PARAGRAPH_106765: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:3]
PARAGRAPH_106766: EBA EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:3]
PARAGRAPH_106767: Executive summary

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:3]
PARAGRAPH_106768: These guidelines aim to achieve convergence of the practices followed by institutions for stress testing across the EU. They provide detailed guidance to be complied with by institutions when designing and conducting a stress testing programme/framework. The EBA issues these guidelines to update and replace the Committee of European Banking Supervisors (CEBS) Guidelines on stress testing (GL32), which will be repealed after the revised guidelines have entered into force.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:3]
PARAGRAPH_106769: These guidelines take into account the conclusions of the peer review of the implementation of GL32.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:3] [RISK:FOREIGN_EXCHANGE_RISK] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106770: The guidelines establish and develop the following concepts: the taxonomy of stress testing; the description of types of stress test exercises; the reverse stress testing process for both regular stress testing and recovery planning purposes; and additional issues that have gained importance in the stress testing programme and need to be incorporated and properly defined, such as conduct- related risk and litigation costs, foreign exchange risk, interaction between solvency stress tests and liquidity stress tests, business models and data aggregation.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:3]
PARAGRAPH_106771: These guidelines recognise the principle of proportionality (see section 4.5) in both the quantitative and the qualitative aspects of stress testing: small and less complex institutions may focus more on the qualitative aspects while more sophisticated stress testing techniques are required of larger or more complex institutions. Stress testing requires a certain frequency to be a meaningful part of an institution's risk management framework. Such frequency should be determined having regard not only to the scope and type of the stress test but also to the nature, scale, size and complexity of the institution's activities (proportionality principle), among other aspects. Moreover, regarding scope and coverage, stress tests should capture risks at various levels in an institution. In this regard, according to the proportionality principle, the scope of stress testing may vary from simple portfolio level sensitivity or individual risk level analyses to comprehensive institution-wide scenario stress testing.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:3]
PARAGRAPH_106772: The EBA launched a first consultation on its draft guidelines during the first quarter of 2016 and received 12 responses to the draft guidelines. The EBA assessed all the main arguments presented in the responses, with a view to deciding on whether or not amendments were required before issuing the final guidelines. The result of this assessment is presented in an extensive feedback section.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:3]
PARAGRAPH_106773: In April 2017, the EBA issued a roadmap outlining its plans to update the common European framework for the supervisory review and evaluation process (SREP) in 2017-2018. Given the close links between Pillar 2 Guidance (P2G) and wider aspects of supervisory stress testing (e.g. the specification of what forms of supervisory stress testing can be used to set or update P2G), the revision of the SREP guidelines also incorporated elements from the first draft of the stress testing guidelines, in particular section 5, 'Supervisory assessment of institutions stress testing'; section 6, 'Supervisory stress testing'; and section 7, 'Use of quantitative results for capital adequacy assessment purposes', which were also reviewed to reflect comments received in the public

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:4] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106775: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:4]
PARAGRAPH_106777: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:4]
PARAGRAPH_106778: consultation. This approach was intended to ensure consistent coverage and the use of various aspects of supervisory stress testing in SREP, which is also an intention of Article 100 of the Capital Requirements Directive (CRD).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:4]
PARAGRAPH_106779: Next steps

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:4] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106780: The guidelines were published for a three-month public consultation, which ended in February 2018. They incorporate the outcomes of the consultation and will be translated into the official EU languages and published on the EBA website. The deadline for competent authorities to report whether or not they comply with the guidelines will be two months after the publication of the translations. The application date will be in 2019.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106782: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5]
PARAGRAPH_106783: EBA EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5]
PARAGRAPH_106784: Background and rationale

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5]
PARAGRAPH_106785: The EBA is mandated to foster sound and effective supervision across the EU arising from the requirements specified in Directive 2013/36/EU and more generally from its obligations under its founding regulation (Regulation (EU) No 1093/2010, the EBA Regulation).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5]
PARAGRAPH_106786: The relevant provisions legally supporting the issuance of the revised guidelines are the provisions of Article 16 of the EBA Regulation and the relevant principles set out in Regulation (EU) No 575/2013 and Directive 2013/36/EU.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106787: Article 16 of Regulation (EU) No 1093/2010 provides that the EBA shall, with a view to establishing consistent, efficient and effective supervisory practices within the European System of Financial Supervision (ESFS), and to ensuring the common, uniform and consistent application of Union law, issue guidelines and recommendations addressed to competent authorities or financial institutions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5] [RISK:LIQUIDITY_RISK] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106788: Institutions are required to take a forward-looking view in their risk management, strategic planning, capital planning and liquidity planning as part of their internal capital adequacy assessment process (ICAAP) required by Article 73 of Directive 2013/36/EU. One of the tools that institutions can use to facilitate this forward-looking perspective in risk management is stress testing.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106789: Since 2010, when the CEBS Guidelines on stress testing (GL32) were issued, there have been a number of developments in stress testing with regard to its methodologies and usage. The financial crisis and several negative events in the financial sector since 2010 have highlighted significant lessons in relation to stress testing practices. Supervisory expectations in relation to institutions' stress testing practices have changed in light of this recent experience both within and beyond the EU. Several important conclusions were drawn from the 2013 EBA peer review on the implementation of the stress testing guidelines. The aim of the peer review performed by the EBA was to assess and compare the effectiveness of the supervisory activities related to the review of credit institutions' own stress testing programmes/frameworks across the EU, as well as the implementation of related provisions by competent authorities1. In particular the results of the peer review suggested that all competent authorities' organisational and resource models had benefits; however, irrespective of the model, dedicated technical experts in stress testing should have been involved. Competent authorities have often focused on the largest institutions in their respective jurisdictions, and devoted far less attention to other institutions. Very few competent authorities required reverse stress testing, and, when they did, it was often only as part of recovery planning. Moreover, the incorporation of the outcomes of stress testing into the supervisory review and evaluation process (SREP) and the joint decision process on institution-specific prudential requirements for cross-border groups was handled differently across jurisdictions. Many of the competent authorities assessments have shown evidence of substantial work on top-down stress testing, from both a micro- and a macroprudential perspective.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5]
PARAGRAPH_106790: For example, in many instances, competent authorities observed that stress testing was not sufficiently integrated into the institutions' risk management frameworks or senior management decision-making. In general, where stress testing was used, scenarios continued to be insufficiently severe. In other

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:5]
PARAGRAPH_106791: 1 https://www.eba.europa.eu/-/eba-publishes-peer-review-on-the-implementation-of-the-stress-testing-guidelines

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:6] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106793: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:6]
PARAGRAPH_106795: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:6]
PARAGRAPH_106796: instances, competent authorities observed that risk concentrations and feedback effects were not considered by institutions in a meaningful fashion.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:6]
PARAGRAPH_106797: These guidelines aim to address deficiencies identified in the EBA peer review, and will assist institutions in understanding the supervisory expectations of appropriate stress testing governance and infrastructure, and also cover the use of stress testing as a risk management tool. These guidelines are designed to identify the relevant building blocks required for an effective stress testing programme, from simple sensitivity analysis on single risk factors or portfolios to complex macroeconomic scenario stress testing on an institution-wide basis.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:6]
PARAGRAPH_106798: While institutions' stress testing is a risk management tool that has been used for a long time, there remains substantial ambiguity and overlap in several terms and definitions. These guidelines, therefore, provide a taxonomy.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:6]
PARAGRAPH_106799: In addition, in recent years, some issues have gained importance in stress testing programmes and need to be incorporated and properly defined, such as the role of reverse stress testing in recovery planning. Moreover, new individual risk categories are covered. Furthermore, business models, data aggregation, the links between solvency stress tests and liquidity stress tests, and other concepts have been updated, as GL32, issued in 2010, have become outdated and do not reflect best industry practices.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:6] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106800: The institutions' stress testing section focuses on the overarching principles of governance including: (a) stress testing governance structures and their use, including the application of the SREP guidelines on the internal governance of stress testing; (b) data infrastructure, in particular data aggregation capabilities and reporting practices; (c) stress testing scope and coverage, taking into account a multi- layered approach, from simple portfolio level and individual risk level stress testing to comprehensive institution-wide stress testing; (d) possible methodologies considering the importance of undertaking both simple sensitivity analyses and more complex scenario stress testing and the severity of scenarios, and highlighting the importance of qualitative and quantitative approaches to reverse stress testing; (e) a range of, non-exhaustive, individual risk categories that should be taken into account in relation to stress testing with the aim of enhancing risk management and capital planning and liquidity processes; and (f) the application of stress testing programmes, including in relation to the interaction between the outputs of stress tests and management actions and the application for recovery and resolution purposes, and the use of stress tests to assess the viability of an institution's capital plan in adverse circumstances in the context of ICAAP and the internal liquidity adequacy assessment process (ILAAP).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:6]
PARAGRAPH_106801: The principle of proportionality applies to all aspects of these guidelines, including the methodology, as well as the frequency and the degree of detail of the stress tests. These guidelines also recognise the principle of proportionality by describing both quantitative and qualitative aspects of stress testing. Examples of proportionality are provided in some sections in relation to applying these guidelines to institutions of different natures, sizes, complexities and business models, as appropriate.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:6]
PARAGRAPH_106802: The proportionality principle is invoked in these guidelines to discuss the level of sophistication of the stress testing methodologies, practices and infrastructure required in relation to the size, structure and internal organisation (also taking into account the nature, scope and complexity of activities) of an institution. In addition, competent authorities should apply the guidelines taking into account the

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:7] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106804: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:7]
PARAGRAPH_106805: EBA EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:7]
PARAGRAPH_106806: principle of proportionality, for example by taking into account the SREP category to which an institution belongs.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:7]
PARAGRAPH_106807: Thus, these guidelines are applicable in their entirety to Category 1 (systemically important) institutions. Category 2 (less or non-systemic) institutions' compliance with the guidelines depends on their nature, scale and size, and the features and complexity of their activities; particular attention is paid to their domestic or cross-border activities, and the simple or multiple business line nature of their activities, characteristics that need to be reflected in their stress testing.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:7] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106808: For Category 3 and 4 institutions (small and medium-sized institutions), the guidance provided in these guidelines must be followed to the extent that it is proportionate and relevant to their activities, resources and the risk posed to the financial system. The scope of stress testing for these institutions reflects the reduced scope of their activities and the limited risk to the system overall.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:7]
PARAGRAPH_106809: Proportionality criteria should also apply to portfolio level stress tests based on the complexity and relative size of the portfolio under consideration. To decide which portfolios need portfolio stress tests, the overall risk situation should also be taken into account. Nevertheless, no portfolio can be left out when assessing the overall risk situation or conducting a combined stress test, as relatively small risks in less important portfolios may amount to an important risk when addressing the whole institution.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:7] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106810: Parent institutions (including EU parents) are expected to implement these guidelines and set up stress testing programmes covering their own consolidated level and, where applicable, material entities and/or business lines subject to the principles of proportionality, materiality and relevance.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:8] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106812: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

PARAGRAPH_106827: 1. Compliance and reporting obligations

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:10]
PARAGRAPH_106828: Status of these guidelines

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:10] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106829: 1. This document contains guidelines issued pursuant to Article 16 of Regulation (EU) No 1093/20102. In accordance with Article 16(3) of Regulation (EU) No 1093/2010, competent authorities and financial institutions must make every effort to comply with the guidelines.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:10]
PARAGRAPH_106830: 2. Guidelines set out the EBA's view of appropriate supervisory practices within the European System of Financial Supervision or of how Union law should be applied in a particular area. Competent authorities as defined in Article 4(2) of Regulation (EU) No 1093/2010 to whom guidelines apply should comply by incorporating them into their practices as appropriate (e.g. by amending their legal framework or their supervisory processes), including where guidelines are directed primarily at institutions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:10]
PARAGRAPH_106831: Reporting requirements

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:10] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106832: 3. In accordance with Article 16(3) of Regulation (EU) No 1093/2010, competent authorities must notify the EBA that they comply or intend to comply with these guidelines, or otherwise give reasons for non-compliance, by ([dd.mm.yyyy]). In the absence of any notification by this deadline, competent authorities will be considered by the EBA to be non-compliant. Notifications should be sent by submitting the form available on the EBA website to compliance@eba.europa.eu with the reference 'EBA/GL/201x/xx'. Notifications should be submitted by persons with appropriate authority to report compliance on behalf of their competent authorities. Any change in the status of compliance must also be reported to the EBA.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:10]
PARAGRAPH_106833: 4. Notifications will be published on the EBA website, in line with Article 16(3).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:10]
PARAGRAPH_106834: 2 Regulation (EU) No 1093/2010 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 24 November 2010 establishing a European Supervisory Authority (European Banking Authority), amending Decision No 716/2009/EC and repealing Commission Decision 2009/78/EC (OJ L 331, 15.12.2010, p. 12).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106836: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106838: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106839: 2. Subject matter, scope and definitions

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106840: Subject matter and scope of application

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106841: 5. These guidelines aim to provide common organisational requirements, methodologies and processes for the performance of stress testing by institutions, taking into account capital adequacy and risk management, as part of their risk management processes ('institutions' stress testing').

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106842: 6. Within the context of groups, these guidelines also apply to institutions participating in a particular stress testing exercise in accordance with the perimeter of application of that particular stress testing exercise and the level of application set out in Articles 108 and 109 of Directive 2013/36/EU.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106843: 7. The terms 'institution' and 'institution-specific' shall be deemed to refer to an institution on a solo basis, or to the parent institution in a given perimeter of application of a particular stress testing exercise or to the parent institution in a Member State or to the EU parent institution on the basis of the relevant consolidated situation as referred to in Article 4(1)(47) of Regulation (EU) No 575/2013.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106844: Addressees

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106845: 8. These guidelines are addressed to competent authorities and institutions as defined in point (i) of Article 4(2) of Regulation (EU) No 1093/2010 and to financial institutions as defined in Article 4(1) of Regulation (EU) No 1093/2010 which are also institutions in accordance with point 3 of Article 4(1) of Regulation (EU) No 575/2013.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106846: Definitions/taxonomy

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106847: 9. Unless otherwise specified, terms used and defined in Regulation (EU) No 575/2013 and in Directive 2013/36/EU have the same meaning in these guidelines. In addition, for the purposes of these guidelines, the following definitions apply:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106848: (1) Solvency stress test

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106849: means the assessment of the impact of certain developments,

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106850: including macro- or microeconomic scenarios, on the overall capital position of an institution, including on its minimum or additional own funds requirements, by means of projecting

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:11]
PARAGRAPH_106851: the institution's capital resources and requirements, highlighting the institution's vulnerabilities and assessing its

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106853: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106855: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106856: capacity to absorb losses and the impact on its solvency position.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106857: (2) Liquidity stress test

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106858: means the assessment of the impact of certain developments, including macro- or microeconomic scenarios, from a funding and liquidity perspective and shocks on the overall liquidity position of an institution, including on its minimum or additional requirements.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106859: (3) Bottom-up stress test

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106860: means a (solvency or liquidity) stress test with all of the following characteristics:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106861: i. it is carried out by institutions using their own internally developed models;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106862: ii. it is based on the institution's own assumptions or scenarios, with possible conservative constrains by authorities;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106863: iii. it is based on the institution's own data and potentially high level of data granularity, with possible use of external data for some additional information; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106864: iv. it concerns particular portfolios or the institution as a whole, producing detailed results on the potential impact of exposure concentrations, institution linkages and contagion probabilities to the institution's loss rates.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106865: (4) Top-down stress test

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106866: means a (solvency or liquidity) stress test with all of the following characteristics:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106867: i. it is carried out by competent authorities or macroprudential authorities;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106868: ii. it is based on general or systemic (macroprudential) assumptions or scenarios designed by competent or macroprudential authorities and applicable to all relevant institutions;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:12]
PARAGRAPH_106869: iii. competent authorities or macroprudential authorities manage the process and calculate the results with less

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106871: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106872: EBA EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106873: involvement of the institutions than in the case of the bottom-up stress test;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106874: iv. it is based mostly on aggregate institution data and less detailed information, depending on the assumptions of the stress test, or sometimes based on more detailed institution data if deemed necessary by authorities; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106875: V. it enables a uniform and a common framework and comparative assessment of the impact of a given stress testing exercise across institutions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106876: (5) Static balance sheet

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106877: assumption

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106878: means a methodological assumption according to which the impact of the stress test scenarios is to be measured on the assumption of a 'constant balance sheet' and of an 'unchanged or stable business model' throughout the projection period, enhancing the comparability of the results across institutions, thereby:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106879: i. prohibiting from taking into account, for the calculation of the impact of the scenarios, changes in the assets and liabilities of the institution that derive, indicatively, from management actions, increases or work-outs of existing lending or differences in maturities or other characteristics of these assets or liabilities (despite the application of the stress test methodology, which might lead to changes in the size and the composition of the balance sheet, and particularly the capital base, over the projection period, due to, for example, new defaults, impairments, increases of stock or value adjustments of financial assets); and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106880: ii. permitting the inclusion of new assets and liabilities as far as these new items bear the same main characteristics (maturities, risk profiles, etc.) with the excluded ones.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106881: (6) Dynamic balance sheet
assumption

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106882: means a methodological assumption according to which the

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:13]
PARAGRAPH_106883: impact of the stress test scenario is to be measured on the possibility of a non-constant balance sheet and of an evolving business model throughout the projection period. Under the

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106885: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106887: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106888: dynamic balance sheet assumption, the outcome of the stress test reflects a combination of the scenario imposed and the responsive actions taken by the management reducing the comparability of the results across institutions. The extent of responsive actions taken by the management may be constrained or unconstrained (e.g. interventions planned from the start and independent from the scenario and/or conditional on the stress test scenario).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106889: (7) Portfolio level stress test

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106890: means a stress test of individual or several portfolios with the focus on the implications of the shocks from a single risk factor or multiple risk factors.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106891: (8) Sensitivity analysis

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106892: means a stress test that measures the potential impact of a specific single risk factor or simple multi-risk factors, affecting capital or liquidity, to a particular portfolio or to the institution as a whole.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106893: (9) Scenario analysis

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106894: means the assessment of the resilience of an institution or of a portfolio to a given scenario that comprises a set of risk factors, which should have all of the following characteristics:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106895: i. they are aligned in an internally consistent way;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106896: ii. the risk factors forming the relevant set presuppose the simultaneous occurrence of forward-looking events covering a range of risks and business areas; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106897: iii. the set of risk factors also aim to reveal, to the maximum extent possible, the nature of linked risks across portfolios and across time, system-wide interactions and feedback effects.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106898: (10) Reverse stress test

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:14]
PARAGRAPH_106899: means an institution stress test that starts from the identification of the pre-defined outcome (e.g. points at which an institution business model becomes unviable, or at which the institution can be considered as failing or likely to fail in the meaning of Article 32 of Directive 2014/59/EU) and then explores scenarios and circumstances that might cause this to occur. Reverse stress testing should have one or more of the following characteristics:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106901: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106902: EBA EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106903: i. it is used as a risk management tool aimed at increasing the institution's awareness of its vulnerabilities by means of the institution explicitly identifying and assessing the scenarios (or a combination of scenarios) that result in a pre-defined outcome;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106904: ii. the institution decides on the kind and timing (triggering events) of management or other actions necessary for both (a) rectifying business failures or other problems; and (b) aligning its risk appetite with the actual risks revealed by the reverse stress testing;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106905: iii. specific reverse stress testing can be also applied in the context of recovery planning (e.g. reverse stress tests applied in a wider context can be used to inform a recovery plan stress test by identifying the conditions under which the recovery might need to be planned).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106906: (11) Second-round or feedback effects

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106907: means the spillover effects (the nature of feedback effects is not limited to macroeconomic effects) caused by the responses of individual institutions to an external original shock, which - in aggregate - generally amplify (it may also mitigate) such an original shock, thereby causing an additional negative feedback loop.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106908: (12) Severity of scenario

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106909: means the degree of severity of the assumptions or the deterioration of the scenario (from baseline to an adverse scenario) expressed in terms of the underlying macroeconomic and financial variables (or any other assumptions). The greater the severity of the scenario, in general, the larger the impact of the stress test on the institution, thereby determining the actual severity of the stress test.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106910: (13) Plausibility of scenario

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:15]
PARAGRAPH_106911: means the degree to which a scenario can be regarded as likely to materialise in respect of the consistency of the relationship of that scenario with the current macroeconomic and financial variables, the support of the scenario by a coherent narrative and the backing of the scenario by probability distribution and historical experiences. Plausibility is not restricted to historical

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:16] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106913: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:16]
PARAGRAPH_106915: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:16]
PARAGRAPH_106916: experiences, and hence expert judgements that take into account changing risk environments (e.g. observed structural breaks) and stress events that were observed in similar risk environments outside the institution's own direct historical experience should play a key role. It is also possible to use simulative methods (e.g. Monte Carlo simulations).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:16]
PARAGRAPH_106917: (14) Anchor scenario

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:16]
PARAGRAPH_106918: means a type of scenario usually designed by a competent authority to set the severity standard for a particular stress test, which is imposed on institutions, either as the scenario that should be applied in the stress test or as a severity benchmark for the development of the institution's own scenarios.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:16]
PARAGRAPH_106919: (15) Risk data aggregation

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:16] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106920: means defining, gathering and processing risk data according to the institution's risk reporting requirements to enable the institution to measure its performance against its risk tolerance/appetite. This includes sorting, merging or breaking down sets of data.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:16]
PARAGRAPH_106921: (16) Data infrastructure

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:16] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106922: means physical and organisational structures and facilities to build and maintain data and information technology (IT) architecture to support the institution's risk data aggregation and internal policy on risk reporting.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:17] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106924: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:17]
PARAGRAPH_106926: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:17]
PARAGRAPH_106927: 3. Implementation

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:17]
PARAGRAPH_106928: Date of application

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:17]
PARAGRAPH_106929: 10. These guidelines apply from 01 January 2019.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:17]
PARAGRAPH_106931: 11. The following guidelines are repealed with effect from the date of publication of these guidelines in all EU official languages.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:17]
PARAGRAPH_106932: - CEBS Guidelines on stress testing (GL32)3

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:17]
PARAGRAPH_106933: 3 https://www.eba.europa.eu/documents/10180/16094/ST Guidelines.pdf

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106935: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106937: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106938: 4. Institutions' stress testing

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106939: 4.1 Stress testing programme

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106940: 12. Institutions should have in place a stress testing programme that should cover at least the following:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106941: a) the types of stress testing and their main objectives and applications;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106942: b) the frequency of the different stress testing exercises;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106943: c) the internal governance arrangements including well-defined, transparent and consistent lines of responsibility and procedures;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106944: d) in the case of a group, the scope of the entities included and the coverage (e.g. risk types and portfolios) of the stress tests;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106945: e) the relevant data infrastructure;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106946: f) the methodological details, including models used and possible links between liquidity stress tests and solvency stress tests, namely the magnitude of such dynamic interactions and the capture of feedback effects;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106947: g) the range of assumptions, including business and managerial, and remedial actions envisaged for each stress test.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106948: 13. Parent institutions in a Member State and EU parent institutions should also develop a group stress testing programme to be approved and monitored by the management body and implemented by their senior management in the context of their centralised risk management policy. A group stress testing programme should include and address, to the extent appropriate, all institutions subject to prudential consolidation.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106949: 14. The institutions within the scope of prudential consolidation should, when establishing their individual stress testing programmes, take into account the relevant group stress testing programme.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18]
PARAGRAPH_106950: 15. Institutions should also include reverse stress testing and reverse stress testing scenarios in their stress testing programmes.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106951: 16. Institutions should ensure that their stress testing programmes are workable and feasible and that they inform decision-making at all appropriate management levels about all existing and potential material risks.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:18] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106952: 17. Institutions should regularly assess their stress testing programmes to determine their effectiveness and robustness, and should update them as appropriate. The assessment should be made on at least an annual basis and on the basis of both a quantitative and a qualitative analysis, and should fully reflect the changing external and internal conditions. Institutions

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106954: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106956: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106957: should ensure that the frequency of assessments takes into account the frequency of the corresponding stress test applications.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19] [RISK:CREDIT_RISK] [RISK:MARKET_RISK] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106958: 18. Institutions should ensure that their quantitative analysis in accordance with the previous paragraph includes sound quantitative tests as backtesting tools to validate the assumptions, parameters and results of stress testing models (e.g. credit risk models, market risk models, pre-provision net revenue models). Institutions should ensure that their qualitative analysis in accordance with the previous paragraph is based on expert judgements or benchmarking assessments.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106959: 19. When assessing the stress testing programme, the institution shall consider at least the following:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106960: a) the effectiveness of the programme in meeting its intended purposes;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106961: b) the need for improvements;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106962: c) the identified risk factors, definitions and reasoning for relevant scenarios, model assumptions and the sensitivity of results to these assumptions, as well as the role of expert judgement to ensure that it is accompanied by sound analysis;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106963: d) the model performance, including its performance on out-of-sample data, i.e. on data that was not used for model development;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106964: e) how to incorporate possible solvency-liquidity adverse loops;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106965: f) the adequacy of possible interlinkages between solvency stress tests and liquidity stress tests;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106966: g) feedback received from competent authorities in the context of their supervisory or other stress tests;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106967: h) the adequacy of the data infrastructure (systems implementation and data quality);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106968: i) the proper level of involvement of senior management and the management body;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106969: j) all assumptions including business and/or managerial assumptions, and management actions envisaged, based on the purpose, type and result of the stress testing, including an assessment of the feasibility of management actions in stress situations and a changing business environment; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106970: k) the adequacy of the relevant documentation.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106971: 20. The institution's stress testing programme should be appropriately documented for all types of stress tests carried out at the single risk type and/or portfolio level, as well as the firm-wide level. Documentation should cover at least:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106972: a) the stress testing approach;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:19]
PARAGRAPH_106973: b) the possible interlinkages between solvency stress tests and liquidity stress tests, namely a mapping between the deterioration on capital position (solvency) and ability to issue commercial paper and bonds (liquidity), macro-driven probabilities of default shifts

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106975: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106977: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106978: (solvency) and the implied rating migration of banks unencumbered assets and the effect on collateral deposited at the relevant central bank (liquidity), the increase in expected non-performing loans (solvency) and the reduction in expected inflows from loan repayments or from non-financial corporation bonds (liquidity), or a possible liquidity gap (liquidity) and asset fire sales (solvency), and an increase in funding costs (liquidity) and P&L effects (solvency);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106979: c) the roles and responsibilities as determined in the internal policy, specifying the roles for the second and third lines of defence, and processes for at least the performance of the stress testing programme;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106980: d) a description of the entire process of designing, approving, performing, monitoring the performance and periodically assessing the stress testing programme and its outcomes;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106981: e) a description of the processes for evaluating stress test outcomes, including details of areas that require manual or human judgemental in some parts, and also of the process for using the results for informing management actions and the strategy of the institution; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106982: f) a description and inventory of the relevant IT applications used for stress testing (and where a central inventory exists, reference can be made to it).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106983: 21. The stress testing programme should be challenged across the organisation, for instance by the risk committee and internal auditors. Business units not responsible for the design and application of the programme and/or non-involved external experts should play a key role in the assessment of this process, taking into account the relevant expertise for specific subjects.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106984: 22. Institutions should ensure, both for the initial design and for the assessment of the stress testing programme, that an effective dialogue has taken place with the involvement of experts from all business areas of the institution and that the programme and its updates have been properly reviewed by the senior management4 and management body of the institution, who are also responsible for monitoring its execution and oversight.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106985: 4.2 Governance aspects of stress testing

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106986: 23. The management body should approve5 the stress testing programme of the institution and oversee its implementation and performance.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106987: 24. Without prejudice to the requirement under Article 91(1) of Directive 2013/36/EU 6 that members of the management body must have at all times sufficient knowledge, skills and experience to perform their duties, the institution should ensure that their management body

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106988: 4 See also Title II, section 1, of the EBA Guidelines on Internal Governance.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106989: See also Title II, section 1, of the EBA Guidelines on Internal Governance.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:20]
PARAGRAPH_106990: 6 See also Title III, section 8, of the Joint ESMA and EBA Guidelines on the assessment of the suitability of members of the management body and key function holders under Directive 2013/36/EU and Directive 2014/65/EU.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106992: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21]
PARAGRAPH_106993: EBA EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21]
PARAGRAPH_106994: is able to fully understand the impact of stress events on the overall risk profile of the institution.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21]
PARAGRAPH_106995: 25. The management body should understand the material aspects of the stress testing programme to be able to:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21]
PARAGRAPH_106996: (a) actively engage in discussions with stress testing committees of the institutions, where applicable, or with senior management or external consultants involved in stress testing;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21]
PARAGRAPH_106997: (b) challenge key modelling assumptions, the scenario selection and the assumptions underlying the stress tests in general; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21]
PARAGRAPH_106998: (c) decide on the necessary management actions and discuss them with the competent authorities.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_106999: 26. The stress testing programme should be executed in accordance with the relevant internal policies and procedures of the institution. The management body of the institution should ensure that clear responsibilities and sufficient resources (e.g. skilled human resources and information technology systems) are assigned and allocated for the execution of the programme.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107000: 27. Institutions should ensure that all elements of the stress testing programme, including its assessment, are appropriately documented and regularly updated, where relevant, in the internal policies and procedures.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107001: 28. Institutions should ensure that the stress testing programme is effectively communicated across business lines and managements levels, with a view to raising awareness, improving risk culture and instigating discussions on existing and potential risks as well as on possible management actions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21]
PARAGRAPH_107002: 29. The stress testing programme should be an integral part of an institution's risk management framework (including in the context of the internal capacity adequacy assessment process (ICAAP) and internal liquidity adequacy assessment process (ILAAP)). Stress tests should support different business decisions and processes as well as strategic planning, including capital and liquidity planning. The decisions should take into account the shortcomings, limitations and vulnerabilities during stress testing.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21]
PARAGRAPH_107003: 30. The management body should take the outcomes of the stress tests into account, in particular with regard to identified limitations, vulnerabilities and shortcomings detected, when setting the institutions strategy and when making all relevant decisions affecting capital, liquidity, recovery and resolution planning.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:21]
PARAGRAPH_107004: 31. The outputs of stress tests (quantitative and qualitative) should be used as inputs to the process of establishing an institution's risk appetite and limits. Furthermore, they should act as a planning tool to determine the effectiveness of new and existing business strategies and their impact on the use of capital. To enable that, the essential outputs from a stress testing exercise should be implied losses, capital and liquidity requirements, as well as available capital and liquidity.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107006: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22]
PARAGRAPH_107008: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22]
PARAGRAPH_107009: 32. To be a meaningful part of the risk management system of an institution, stress tests should be undertaken with appropriate frequency. This frequency should be determined having regard to the scope and type of the stress test, the nature, scale, size and complexity of the institution (proportionality principle), portfolio characteristics as well as changes in the macroeconomic environment or the institution's business activities.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22]
PARAGRAPH_107010: 4.3 Data infrastructure

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107011: 33. Institutions should ensure that the stress testing programme is supported by an adequate data infrastructure.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107012: 34. To ensure that a proper data infrastructure has been put in place, institutions, including those that are not global systemically important institutions (G-SIIs), should endeavour to also refer, to the extent appropriate, to the principles for effective risk data aggregation and risk reporting of the Basel Committee on Banking Supervision7.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107013: 35. Institutions should ensure that their data infrastructure has the capacity to capture the extensive data needs of their stress testing programme and that they have in place mechanisms to ensure their continuing ability to conduct stress testing as planned in accordance with the programme.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107014: 36. Institutions should ensure that the data infrastructure allows for both flexibility and appropriate levels of quality and control.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107015: 37. Institutions should ensure that their data infrastructure is proportionate to their size, complexity, and risk and business profile, and allows for the performance of stress tests covering all material risks that the institution is exposed to.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22]
PARAGRAPH_107016: 38. Institutions should devote sufficient human, financial and material resources to guarantee the effective development and maintenance of their data infrastructure, including information technology systems.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22]
PARAGRAPH_107017: 39. Institutions should also consider stress testing data infrastructure as part of their overall information technology infrastructure and should give adequate consideration to business continuity planning, the identification of long-term investments and other IT processes.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22]
PARAGRAPH_107018: Data aggregation capabilities for stress testing purposes

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107019: 40. Institutions should maintain and keep up-to-date accurate and reliable risk data to conduct reliable stress tests and should also have in place a dedicated process for aggregating and producing such data.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:22]
PARAGRAPH_107020: 7 http://www.bis.org/publ/bcbs239.pdf

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107022: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107024: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107025: 41. Institutions should ensure that their aggregation of risk data is characterised by accuracy and integrity, completeness, timeliness and adaptability.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107026: 42. Institutions should ensure that data are aggregated on a largely automated basis so as to minimise the probability of error. In particular, a thorough reconciliation and controls system should be in place.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107027: 43. Institutions should have the capacity to guarantee the completeness of risk data. For that purpose, institutions should ensure that risk data also fully capture off-balance-sheet risks and are easily attainable at any level of the institution. Materiality, in terms of existent and potential risk, should be factored in.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107028: 44. Institutions should be able to produce aggregated risk information on a timely basis to meet all reporting requirements throughout the process of stress testing following different quality assurance and challenge stages; for that purpose, institutions should develop an efficient structure that ensures timeliness.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107029: 45. Institutions should be able to generate aggregate data to meet a broad range of on-demand requests arising both from internal needs in the institution and externally from supervisory queries.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107030: Reporting practices for stress testing purposes

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107031: 46. Institutions should ensure that their risk reporting process:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107032: a) is completely supported by data aggregation capabilities;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107033: b) accurately and precisely conveys aggregated risk data and reflects risk in an exact manner;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107034: c) covers all material risks and, in particular, allows the identification of emerging vulnerabilities that could potentially be further assessed even in the same stress testing exercise;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107035: d) offers or is able to offer additional information regarding main assumptions, tolerance levels or caveats; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107036: e) communicates information in a clear and concise manner including meaningful information tailored to the needs of the recipients.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107037: 4.4 Stress testing scope and coverage

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107038: 4.4.1 General requirements

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:23]
PARAGRAPH_107039: 47. Stress tests should take into account all types of material risk having regard to both the on- and off-balance-sheet assets and liabilities of an institution including relevant structured entities.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107041: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107042: EBA EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107043: 48. Stress tests should capture risks at various levels in an institution. In this regard, according to the proportionality principle, the scope of stress testing may vary from simple portfolio level sensitivity or individual risk level analyses to comprehensive institution-wide scenario stress testing.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107044: 49. Stress tests should take into account changes in correlations between risk types and risk factors, at individual entity and at a group-wide level. They should also take into account that correlations tend to increase during times of economic or financial distress and that case-by- case analyses of how certain correlations behave in certain scenarios are required.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107045: 4.4.2 Portfolio and individual risk level stress testing

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107046: 50. Institutions should perform stress tests on an individual portfolio basis, covering all risk types that affect these portfolios, using both sensitivity and scenario analyses. Institutions should also identify risk factors and their adequate level of stress, wherever possible, at the level of an individual portfolio.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107047: 51. Institutions should ensure that they stress test portfolios and business lines or units to identify intra- and inter-risk concentrations - i.e. concentrations of common risk factors within and across risk types (including contagion effects).

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24] [RISK:CREDIT_RISK]
PARAGRAPH_107048: 52. In particular, when considering inter-risk concentrations, institutions should aggregate across risk types notably market and credit risk, to gain a better understanding of their potential risk concentrations in a stress situation. Institutions should identify potential links between exposures that could be risky during periods of economic or financial distress, as well as question assumptions about dependencies and correlations between risk types in a stress situation.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107049: 4.4.3 Institution-wide stress testing

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107050: 53. In order to deliver a complete and holistic picture of the institution's risks, in addition to stress tests on the level of single entities, stress testing should also be conducted at the group level and across portfolios and individual risk types.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107051: 54. It should be taken into account that:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107052: a) risks at the institution-wide level may not be well reflected by a simple aggregation of stress tests on portfolios, individual risk areas or business units of the group;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24]
PARAGRAPH_107053: b) correlations, offsetting of individual exposures and concentrations may lead to either the double counting of risks or to an underestimation of the impact of stressed risk factors; and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:24] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107054: c) specific group risks may arise at the institution-wide level and, therefore, institutions should ensure that all material risks and their corresponding risk factors are also identified at an institution-wide level; when looking at risks at an institution-wide level, particular attention should be paid to risk concentrations on a holistic basis.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107056: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107058: EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107059: 55. A group or an institution that is internationally active should also perform stress tests at the level of business units in specific geographical regions or business sectors or business lines to account for differing risk factors in different businesses and regions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107060: 4.5 Proportionality

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107061: 56. In accordance with the principle of proportionality, an institution's stress testing programme should be consistent with its individual risk profile and business model.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107062: 57. Institutions should take into account their size and internal organisation, and the nature, scale and complexity of their activities when developing and implementing a stress testing programme. Significant institutions and more complex institutions, including at consolidated level, should have more sophisticated stress testing programmes, while small and less complex institutions and groups (consolidated level) may implement simpler stress testing programmes.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107063: 58. For the purpose of the application of the principle of proportionality and in order to ensure an appropriate implementation of the requirements, the following criteria should be taken into account by institutions and competent authorities:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107064: a) the size in terms of the balance-sheet total or the quantity of assets held by the institution or its subsidiaries within the scope of prudential consolidation;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107065: b) the geographical presence of the institution and the size of its operations in each jurisdiction;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107066: c) the legal form and whether or not the institution is part of group and, if so, the proportionality assessment performed for the group;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107067: d) whether the institution is listed or not;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107068: e) whether or not the institution is authorised to use internal models for the measurement of capital requirements (e.g. the internal ratings-based (IRB) approach);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107069: f) the type of authorised activity and services (e.g. loans and deposits, investment banking);

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107070: g) the underlying business model and strategy, the nature and complexity of the business activities, and the organisational structure;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107071: h) the risk strategy, risk appetite and actual risk profile of the institution, also taking into account the result of the annual capital adequacy assessment;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107072: i) the ownership structure and funding structure of the institution;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107073: j) ) the type of clients (e.g. retail, corporate, institutional, small businesses, public entity) and the complexity of the products or contracts;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107074: k) the outsourced processes, services and activities and their distribution channels;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:25]
PARAGRAPH_107075: l) the existing information technology systems, including IT continuity systems and outsourcing arrangements in this area, e.g. cloud computing.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107077: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26]
PARAGRAPH_107078: EBA EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26]
PARAGRAPH_107079: 4.6 Stress testing types

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26]
PARAGRAPH_107080: 4.6.1 General requirements

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26]
PARAGRAPH_107081: 59. The specific design, complexity and level of detail of the stress test methodologies should be appropriate to the institution's nature, scale and size, as well as the complexity and riskiness of its business activities. It should take into account the strategy and business model as well as the portfolio characteristics of the institution.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26]
PARAGRAPH_107082: 60. Institutions should take into account the stage within the economic cycle when designing stress test methodologies, including the scenario and the need for possible management actions.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26]
PARAGRAPH_107083: 61. Institutions should identify appropriate, meaningful and robust mechanisms for translating risk factors into relevant internal risk parameters (probability of default (PD), loss given default (LGD), write-offs, fair value haircuts, etc.) that provide an institution and a group view of risks.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26]
PARAGRAPH_107084: 62. The link between stressed risk factors and the risk parameters not only should be based on institutional historical experience and analysis, but should be supplemented, where available and appropriate, with benchmarks from external sources and, when possible, from supervisory guidance.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26] [RISK:MODEL_RISK] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107085: 63. Because of the complexity involved in modelling hypothetical and macroeconomic-based risk factors/scenarios, institutions should be aware of the model risk involved and ensure that the following have been performed when setting those factors/scenarios:

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26] [RISK:MODEL_RISK]
PARAGRAPH_107086: a) a regular and sufficiently conservative expert review of the model's assumptions and mechanics has been performed and a conservative modelling approach to account for model risk has been followed;

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107087: b) a sufficient degree of conservatism as appropriate has been applied when making assumptions that are difficult to measure in a quantitative way (e.g. diversification, exponential growth projected, fees projected, forward-looking management views) but may have an impact on the model's outputs (e.g. the outputs of pre-provision net revenue models should be based on sufficient statistical support as well as business considerations); and

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26]
PARAGRAPH_107088: c) the dependencies and sensitivities of the results on the assumptions have been acknowledged and their impact is assessed on a regular basis.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:26]
PARAGRAPH_107089: 64. Shortcomings of models and mechanisms that link risk factors with losses or increased risk parameters should be understood, communicated clearly and taken into account when interpreting results. Models should take into account the interactions between solvency and funding liquidity and funding costs in order to not systemically and significantly underestimate the impact of a shock. Where possible, results for different modelling approaches should be compared (e.g. for pre-provision net revenue models, a comparison between the model used and other possible approaches and the rationale for their rejection should be available). These

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107091: FINAL REPORT ON GUIDELINES ON INSTITUTIONS' STRESS TESTING

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_107092: EBA EUROPEAN BANKING AUTHORITY

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_107093: links should be based on robust statistical models. However, if data availability or quality or structural breaks in historical data do not allow for meaningful estimates (e.g. for pre-provision net revenue models, it is necessary to have historical data covering an interest rate cycle and a business cycle, as well as information on changes in business strategy and organisation structure), quantitative analyses should be supported with qualitative expert judgements. Even where the underlying modelling process is robust, expert judgement should play a role in challenging model outputs.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107094: 65. Institutions should assess possible non-linear interactions between risk factors and stressed risk parameters.

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27]
PARAGRAPH_107095: 4.6.2 Sensitivity analysis

[JURISDICTION:EU] [SOURCE:EBA] [CATEGORY:FINANCIAL_REGULATION] [PAGE:27] [REQ_TYPE:MANDATORY]
PARAGRAPH_107096: 66. Institutions should conduct sensitivity analyses at the level of individual exposures, portfolios or business units, institution wide, and for specific risk types, proportionate to their complexity.
